[3:0:344,435] Governmental bodies classified under the  

[4:0:344,445] Legislative, Judicial, and Executive section of the  

[4:1:344,455] Governor's Budget are either established as  

[4:2:344,465] independent entities under the California  

[5:0:344,475] Constitution, or are departments with a recognized  

[5:1:344,485] need to operate outside of the administrative  

[5:2:344,495] oversight and control of an agency secretary.  

[5:3:344,505] Constitutionally-established bodies include the  

[5:4:344,515] Legislature, Judicial Branch, Governor's Office,  

[5:5:344,525] and constitutional officers. This section also  

[6:0:344,534] includes such independent entities as the Office of  

[6:1:344,544] the Inspector General and the California State  

[6:2:344,554] Lottery Commission.

[1:0:268,39] 0110   Senate  

[2:0:66,60] The Legislature is comprised of two houses, the Senate and the Assembly, and is responsible for enacting laws and  

[2:1:66,70] establishing public policy for California. The State Senate is comprised of 40 members who are elected for 4-year terms.  

[2:2:66,79] Members of the Legislature may serve a maximum of 12 years total in the Senate, the Assembly, or both, in any combination of  

[2:3:66,89] terms. Members first elected before June 6, 2012, however, may generally serve a maximum of 14 years total, with no more  

[2:4:66,99] than two terms in the Senate and three terms in the Assembly.

[4:0:243,130] 0130   Joint Expenses  

[5:0:66,151] The Legislature is comprised of two houses, the Senate and the Assembly, and is responsible for enacting laws and  

[5:1:66,160] establishing public policy for California. Both houses contribute to support the Legislative Analyst's Office, which provides fiscal  

[5:2:66,170] and policy advice to the Legislature, and is overseen by the 16-member bipartisan Joint Legislative Budget Committee.  

[5:3:66,188] Because the Legislature's   programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Legislature has a capital outlay program to  

[5:4:66,197] support this need.   For the specifics on the Legislature's   capital outlay program see "Infrastructure Overview."

[16:0:66,652] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW  

[17:0:66,671] The California State Capitol, which serves as the state’s working seat of government, began construction in 1860 and was  

[17:1:66,681] completed in 1874. The Capitol remained largely unchanged until 1949, when additional space requirements drove the need for  

[17:2:66,691] construction of the Capitol Annex, which attaches to the east side of the original Capitol building.   The Annex, which was  

[17:3:66,700] completed in 1951, houses legislative offices, committee rooms, and the Governor’s offices.

[10:0:196,412] 0150   Contributions to the Legislators  

[11:0:66,433] Established in 1947, the Legislators' Retirement System provides retirement and death benefits for legislators, constitutional  

[11:1:66,442] officers, and legislative statutory officers.  

[12:0:66,462] The California Public Employees' Retirement System (CalPERS) administers the Legislators' Retirement System on behalf of  

[12:1:66,472] its members. Retirement benefits paid are based upon age, years of service, and final compensation. Benefits for death,  

[12:2:66,482] disability, and surviving dependents of deceased members are also provided under specific conditions.   The Legislators'  

[12:3:66,491] Retirement System is funded through contributions from the state, members of the system, and investment earnings. 

[13:0:66,511] Proposition 140, approved by voters in 1990, closed the Legislators' Retirement System to all new legislators after November  

[13:1:66,521] 6, 1990.   Subsequently, the California Public Employees' Pension Reform Act of 2013, Chapter 296, Statutes of 2012 (AB 340)  

[13:2:66,530] closed the Legislators' Retirement System to all new members effective January 1, 2013. New constitutional officers, statutory  

[13:3:66,540] officers, Sergeant-at-Arms, and the Insurance Commissioner retain optional membership rights in CalPERS.

[6:0:208,199] 0160   Legislative Counsel Bureau  

[7:0:66,220] The Legislative Counsel Bureau (Bureau) provides legal services to the two houses of the Legislature, and their members and  

[7:1:66,230] committees, by resolving a large volume of complex legal problems arising in connection with the legislative process. The legal  

[7:2:66,239] services furnished include rendering legal opinions, drafting bills and other legislative measures, counseling, attending  

[7:3:66,249] meetings of legislative committees as counsel, and representing the Legislature in litigation. The Bureau also provides legal  

[7:4:66,259] services to the Governor and advises state agencies as to the preparation of legislative measures. An attorney-client  

[7:5:66,269] relationship is maintained and all work is confidential.  

[8:0:66,288] In addition, the Bureau prepares and provides necessary indices and appropriate tables necessary to identify legislative  

[8:1:66,298] measures and compiles and indexes statutes and codes.  

[9:0:66,318] The Bureau operates the Legislative Data Center, which provides technology services to the Legislature, including IT services  

[9:1:66,327] in support of legislative business operations and the legislative information system, which provides information to the public  

[9:2:66,337] regarding pending legislation and existing law.  

[10:0:66,357] Pursuant to Chapter 46 of the Statutes of 2012, the California Commission on Uniform State Laws was transferred into the  

[10:1:66,366] Bureau. The California Commission on Uniform State Laws presents to the Legislature uniform laws recommended by the  

[10:2:66,376] National Conference of Commissioners on Uniform State Laws and then promotes passage of these uniform acts.  

[10:3:66,393] Pursuant to Chapter 450 of the Statutes of 2018, the Bureau provides advice and investigation services to the Legislature  

[10:4:66,403] related to workplace misconduct through the Workplace Conduct Unit.

[9:0:242,458] 0250   Judicial Branch  

[10:0:66,479] Article VI of the Constitution creates the Supreme Court of California and the Courts of Appeal to exercise the judicial power of  

[10:1:66,489] the state at the appellate level. Article VI also creates the Judicial Council of California to administer the state's judicial system.  

[10:2:66,499] Chapter 869, Statutes of 1997, created the California Habeas Corpus Resource Center to represent any person financially  

[10:3:66,508] unable to employ appellate counsel in capital cases.  

[11:0:66,528] The Lockyer-Isenberg Trial Court Funding Act of 1997 (Chapter 850, Statutes of 1997) provided a stable and consistent  

[11:1:66,538] funding source for the trial courts. Beginning with fiscal year 1997-98, consolidation of the costs of trial court operation was  

[11:2:66,548] implemented at the state level, with the exception of facility, revenue collection, and local judicial benefit costs. This  

[12:0:66,557] implementation capped the counties' general purpose revenue contributions to trial court costs at a revised 1994-95 level. The  

[12:1:66,567] county contributions become part of the Trial Court Trust Fund, which supports all trial court operations. Fine and penalty  

[13:0:66,577] revenue collected by each county is retained or distributed in accordance with statute. Each county makes quarterly payments  

[13:1:66,587] to the Trial Court Trust Fund equal to the fine and penalty revenue received by the state General Fund in 1994-95, as adjusted  

[13:2:66,596] by amounts equivalent to specified fine and fee revenues that counties benefited from in 2003-04. The Trial Court Facilities Act  

[13:3:66,606] of 2002 (Chapter 1082, statutes of 2002) provided a process for the responsibility for court facilities to be transferred from the  

[13:4:66,616] counties to the state by July 1, 2007, which was extended to December 31, 2009, by Chapter 9, Statutes of 2008. The Trial  

[13:5:66,626] Court Facilities Act of 2002 also established several new revenue sources, effective on January 1, 2003. These revenues are  

[13:6:66,635] deposited into the State Court Facilities Construction Fund for the purpose of funding the construction and maintenance of  

[13:7:66,645] court facilities throughout the state. Counties contribute revenues for the ongoing operation and maintenance of court facilities  

[13:8:66,655] based upon historical expenditures for facilities transferred to the state.  

[14:0:66,675] The mission of the Judicial Branch is to resolve disputes arising under the law and to interpret and apply the law consistently,  

[14:1:66,684] impartially, and independently to protect the rights and liberties guaranteed by the Constitutions of California and the United  

[14:2:66,694] States, in a fair, accessible, effective, and efficient manner.  

[15:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[28:0:64,587] 1/ Reflects the 2021-22 4th quarter Quarterly Financial Statement information submitted by the trial courts. A detailed breakdown of this data can be found in the Report of Trial Court Revenue, Expenditure, and Fund Balance Constraints for 2021-22. Non-state  

[28:1:64,593] funding includes local fees and non-fee revenue, enhanced collections and other reimbursements, grants from non-state entities, etc. 

[29:0:64,599] 2/ Reflects the filled full-time equivalent positions reported on the Schedule 7As submitted by the trial courts. Excludes judges who are constitutional officers and not trial court employees. 

[30:0:64,607] 3/ Reflects the preliminary budgets of 57 trial courts based on courts' 2022-23 Schedule 1 submissions. Courts have been noted with an asterisk (*) for when Schedule 1 data from 2021-22 is provided.  

[30:1:64,615] 4/ Reflects pending allocations from the Judicial Council. Trial courts may have budgeted for some of these funds in Section 1 in anticipation of their allocation.  

[31:0:64,622] 5/ See the "State Trial Court Funding Not Distributed to the Trial Courts" (Figure 2) display for more detail. Funds are either disbursed on behalf of trial courts, for statewide programs, for judges compensation, or to non-court entities, and as a result are not included in  

[31:1:64,629] the trial courts’ state funding in Section 1. 

[32:0:64,635] 6/ See the "State Trial Court Funding Not Distributed to the Trial Courts" (Figure 2) display for more detail. These expenses are funded by the trial courts opting to participate in those programs from their "State Funding" revenue distribution amounts reported in  

[33:0:64,641] Section 1 of the "State and Non-State Trial Court Funding, Expenditures, and Positions" (Figure 1) display. Because the funding for these expenses is already included in Section 1, they are subtracted from the total "State Trial Court Funding Not Distributed to Trial  

[33:1:64,646] Courts" (Figure 2) amount used to calculate the total expenditures displayed for the "State Trial Court Funding Total." 

[34:0:64,652] 7/ For the prior year, recognizes that the revenues courts report individually as received or to be received from the state will not be equal to the "State Trial Court Funding" expenditure amount reported at the state level due to timing and accounting differences. For  

[34:1:64,659] the current year, this category reflects either differences in local versus state revenue projections, pending court budgets, or unallocated appropriation.

# === PAGE 25 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:66,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:414,13] 2023-24 STATE BUDGET — LJE   23 

[2:0:207,32] 0250   Judicial Branch - Continued 

[3:0:66,65] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[3:1:66,84] 0130 - SUPREME COURT  

[4:0:66,103] The Supreme Court is the highest court in the California judicial system. Its decisions are binding on all other California state  

[4:1:66,113] courts. The Chief Justice of California and the six Associate Justices entertain petitions seeking review of decisions from the  

[4:2:66,123] Courts of Appeal, original petitions for extraordinary relief (such as writs of mandate or habeas corpus), and recommendations  

[4:3:66,133] for discipline of judicial officers and attorneys. The Court grants review and issues opinions in order to settle legal questions of  

[4:4:66,142] statewide importance. In addition, under the California Constitution, all death penalty judgments are appealed directly to the  

[4:5:66,152] Supreme Court.  

[4:6:66,169] 0135 - COURTS OF APPEAL  

[5:0:66,189] Established by a constitutional amendment in 1904, the Courts of Appeal are California's intermediate courts of review. The six  

[5:1:66,199] District Courts of Appeal hear appeals and original proceedings at nine different locations around the state. Cases before the  

[5:2:66,209] Courts of Appeal involve every area of civil and criminal law.  

[5:3:66,226] 0140 - JUDICIAL COUNCIL  

[6:0:66,245] The Judicial Council of California is the constitutional policy-making body for the state judiciary. The Council consists of 21  

[6:1:66,255] voting members and 9 advisory members; the Chief Justice of California serves as chair. The Judicial Council staff serve as the  

[6:2:66,265] administrative arm of the Council. Staff provide policy support to the Council, administrative accountability in the operation of  

[6:3:66,275] the courts as specified by law, strategic planning for capital outlay, design, and construction of court facilities; and  

[6:4:66,284] administrative support for courts in areas such as budget, fiscal services, coordination of the assignment of retired judges,  

[6:5:66,294] technology, education, legal advice and services, human resources, legislative advocacy, and research.  

[6:6:66,312] 0140023 - JUDICIAL BRANCH FACILITY PROGRAM  

[7:0:66,331] The Judicial Branch Facility Program administers the acquisition, planning, construction, operations, and maintenance of  

[7:1:66,341] judicial branch facilities. This program is responsible for the development of long-term facilities master plans, facility and real  

[7:2:66,351] estate management, renovation of existing court facilities, and new courthouse planning, design, and construction.  

[7:3:66,368] 0150 - STATE TRIAL COURT FUNDING  

[8:0:66,385] California has 58 trial courts, one in each county. In trial courts, or superior courts, a judge and sometimes a jury hears  

[8:1:66,395] witnesses' testimony and other evidence and decides cases by applying the relevant law to the facts.   Trial courts have trial  

[8:2:66,405] jurisdiction over all criminal and civil cases. To accomplish various statutory mandates, the State Trial Court Funding Program  

[8:3:66,414] supports trial courts through the following programs:  

[8:4:66,434] 0150010 - SUPPORT FOR THE OPERATION OF THE TRIAL COURTS  

[9:0:66,451] This program's objective is to provide the resources necessary for the statewide trial court system to adjudicate civil and  

[9:1:66,461] criminal cases. This program includes all allowable trial court administrative costs under Government Code section 77003.  

[9:2:66,478] 0150011 - COURT APPOINTED DEPENDENCY COUNSEL  

[10:0:66,496] This program provides funding for court-appointed counsel for children, non-minor dependents and parents in juvenile court  

[10:1:66,505] dependency proceedings pursuant to Welfare and Institutions Code section 317, subdivisions (b) and (c), and Government  

[10:2:66,515] Code section 77003, subdivision (a)(4).  

[10:3:66,532] 0150019 - COMPENSATION OF SUPERIOR COURT JUDGES  

[10:4:66,550] This program provides funding for the salaries and state benefits for Superior Court judges.  

[10:5:66,567] 0150028 - ASSIGNED JUDGES  

[11:0:66,584] This program provides support for the salaries and related costs of retired as well as active judges who are assigned by the  

[11:1:66,594] Chief Justice to positions in courts which require assistance due to judicial absences or other factors impacting the ability of a  

[11:2:66,604] court to avoid case delay.  

[11:3:66,621] 0150037 - COURT INTERPRETERS  

[12:0:66,638] This program supports the provision of qualified language interpreters in criminal, juvenile, family and civil proceedings as  

[12:1:66,648] required by statute.  

[12:2:66,665] 0150046 - GRANTS  

[13:0:66,683] This program provides funding for government grants providing public services related to the trial courts.  

[13:1:66,700] 0150051 – CHILD SUPPORT COMMISSIONER PROGRAM (AB 1058)  

[14:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[0:0:66,13] 2023-24 STATE BUDGET — LJE   24 

[1:0:382,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[2:0:207,32] 0250   Judicial Branch - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] This program provides funding for Child Support Commissioners and Family Law Facilitators in every court.  

[3:1:66,86] 0150067 – COURT APPOINTED SPECIAL ADVOCATE (CASA) PROGRAM  

[4:0:66,103] This program provides funding for non-profits designated by the court to train and provide volunteers to advocate for children in  

[4:1:66,113] foster care.  

[4:2:66,130] 0150083 – EQUAL ACCESS FUND  

[5:0:66,147] This program provides funding for legal services programs to provide a range of services to low-income litigants.  

[5:1:66,165] 0150095 - EXPENSES ON BEHALF OF THE TRIAL COURT  

[6:0:66,182] This program provides appropriation for statewide programs and services provided to the court or courts by the Judicial Council  

[6:1:66,192] or payment for services or property of any kind contracted for the court or courts or on behalf of the courts by the Judicial  

[6:2:66,201] Council, which are paid for or reimbursed by the trial courts. The appropriation also supports the implementation and  

[6:3:66,211] administration of the Civil Representation Pilot Program.  

[7:0:66,228] In addition to the programs mentioned above, the State Trial Court Funding Program supports a number of smaller programs  

[7:1:66,238] including Access to Visitation services in family law proceedings, JusticeCorps volunteers in the courts, and Substance Abuse  

[7:2:66,248] Focus Grants supporting collaborative justice courts.  

[7:3:66,265] 0155 - HABEAS CORPUS RESOURCE CENTER  

[8:0:66,285] The Habeas Corpus Resource Center provides legal representation for indigent petitioners in death penalty habeas corpus  

[8:1:66,295] proceedings before the California state courts and the federal courts. The Center also serves as a resource center for the  

[8:2:66,304] private capital defense bar, and it   recruits and trains attorneys to expand the pool of private counsel qualified to accept  

[8:3:66,314] appointments in death penalty habeas corpus proceedings,   and thereby helps to reduce the number of unrepresented indigents  

[8:4:66,324] on California's death row.

[11:0:66,655] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW  

[12:0:66,674] The Judicial Branch consists of the Supreme Court, courts of appeal, trial courts, and the Judicial Council. The Supreme Court  

[12:1:66,684] is located in the 103,300 square foot (sf) Civic Center Plaza in San Francisco and the 9,800 sf Ronald Reagan State Building in  

[12:2:66,693] Los Angeles. The courts of appeal are organized into six districts, operate in nine different locations, and consist of  

[12:3:66,703] approximately 538,000 sf. The trial courts are located in 58 counties statewide, in approximately 430 facilities, and 2,200  

[12:4:66,713] courtrooms of approximately 16 million sf of usable area and more than 21 million sf of space under Judicial Council  

[13:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,68] responsibility and management. The facilities of the Supreme Court, courts of appeal, and trial courts encompass not only the  

[3:1:66,78] public courtroom spaces but also the chambers and workspaces where judicial officers and courtroom staff prepare for  

[3:2:66,88] proceedings; secure areas, including holding cells; and building support functions. Judicial Council administrative facilities,  

[3:3:66,98] occupying approximately 248,000 sf, are located in San Francisco and Sacramento.

[5:0:180,246] 0280   Commission on Judicial Performance  

[6:0:66,267] The California Commission on Judicial Performance is the independent state agency responsible for investigating complaints of  

[6:1:66,277] judicial misconduct and judicial incapacity, and for disciplining judges pursuant to Article VI, Section 18 of the California  

[6:2:66,287] Constitution. It is the only body with such authority in the state. Its jurisdiction includes all active judges and justices of  

[6:3:66,297] California's superior courts, Courts of Appeal and Supreme Court, and former judges for conduct prior to retirement or  

[6:4:66,306] resignation. The Commission also shares authority with the local courts for the oversight of court commissioners and referees.  

[6:5:66,316] In addition to its disciplinary functions, the Commission is responsible for handling judges' applications for disability retirement.  

[7:0:66,336] The Commission's authority is limited to investigating alleged judicial misconduct and, if warranted, imposing discipline. Judicial  

[7:1:66,345] misconduct usually involves conduct in conflict with the standards set forth in the Code of Judicial Ethics. After investigation  

[7:2:66,355] and, in some cases a public hearing, the Commission may impose sanctions ranging from confidential discipline to removal  

[7:3:66,365] from office.  

[8:0:66,385] The Commission is composed of 11 members: 3 judges appointed by the Supreme Court; 2 attorneys appointed by the  

[8:1:66,394] Governor; and 6 lay citizens, of which 2 are appointed by the Governor, 2 are appointed by the Senate Committee on Rules,  

[8:2:66,404] and 2 are appointed by the Speaker of the Assembly. Members are appointed to four-year terms and may serve two terms.  

[8:3:66,414] Commission members do not receive a salary.

[10:0:207,507] 0390   Contributions to the Judges  

[11:0:66,528] The Judges' Retirement System provides retirement benefit funding for judges on California's Supreme, Appellate, and  

[11:1:66,538] Superior/Municipal courts. The California Public Employees' Retirement System administers both the Judges' Retirement  

[11:2:66,548] System and the Judges' Retirement System II on behalf of its members.  

[12:0:66,565] The Judges' Retirement System is closed to new members, and a second retirement system for judges was established in  

[12:1:66,575] 1994. All new judges elected or appointed on or after November 9, 1994 become members of the Judges' Retirement System  

[12:2:66,585] II. The Judges' Retirement System II provides retirement, disability, and death benefits based on age, years of service, final  

[12:3:66,594] compensation, and eligibility, as determined by specific sections of the Judges' Retirement System II Law. Judges' Retirement  

[12:4:66,604] System II members eligible for a service retirement have the option of choosing the monetary credit plan (a lump-sum return of  

[12:5:66,614] contributions and interest earned) or the defined benefit plan. Judges' Retirement System II members not eligible for a defined  

[12:6:66,624] benefit receive the balance of their monetary credits (in a lump-sum payment). The Judges' Retirement System II is funded  

[12:7:66,633] through contributions from the state, members of the system, and investment earnings. The state's contributions are adjusted  

[12:8:66,643] annually to maintain actuarial soundness of the fund.  

[13:0:66,663] The Judges' Retirement System provides retirement, disability, and death benefits based on age, years of service,  

[14:0:66,673] compensation of active judges, and eligibility, as determined by specific sections of the Judges' Retirement Law. Active judges  

[14:1:66,682] and the state each contribute 8 percent of salary to the Judges' Retirement System. Additional contributions come from filing  

[14:2:66,692] fees for specific civil cases and investment income. These contributions, however, are not sufficient to fully fund benefit  

[14:3:66,702] payments. Consequently, current law requires the state to fund the difference between existing contribution sources and the  

[14:4:66,712] required benefit payments to retired judges.  

[15:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[4:0:66,484] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:1:66,502] 0220 - GO-Biz  

[5:0:66,522] The GO-Biz serves as the Governor's lead entity for economic strategy and the marketing of California on issues relating to  

[5:1:66,532] business development, private sector investment, and economic growth, and export promotion. This program makes  

[5:2:66,542] recommendations to the Governor and the Legislature regarding policies, programs, and actions to advance statewide  

[5:3:66,551] economic goals.  

[6:0:66,569] 0225 - CALIFORNIA BUSINESS INVESTMENT SERVICES  

[7:0:66,586] This program serves employers, corporate executives, business owners, and site location consultants who are considering  

[7:1:66,596] California for business investment and expansion. This program convenes teams on key business development issues. This  

[7:2:66,605] program works with local, state, and federal partners to attract, retain, and grow businesses in addition to providing permit  

[7:3:66,615] assistance and helping businesses succeed in California.  

[7:4:66,632] 0230 - CALIFORNIA OFFICE OF THE SMALL BUSINESS ADVOCATE  

[8:0:66,650] The California Office of the Small Business Advocate (CalOSBA) serves as the principal advocate in the state on behalf of  

[8:1:66,659] small businesses, including legislation and administrative regulations that affect small business. CalOSBA ensures that  

[8:2:66,669] information, content and direct support are available to minority and small businesses to better navigate state resources,  

[8:3:66,679] programs and services. CalOSBA advocates on behalf of small businesses concerning the actions of state agencies, state  

[8:4:66,689] laws, regulations and procurement opportunities, maintaining the connection to agency small business advocates/liaisons. It  

[8:5:66,699] serves as the co-Coordinator with CalOES for the Economic Recovery Support Function under the California Disaster  

[9:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[1:0:382,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[2:0:89,32] 0509   Governor's Office of Business and Economic Development (GO-Biz) - 

[2:1:276,46] Continued 

[3:0:66,68] Recovery Framework. CalOSBA administers the Technical Assistance Expansion Program and Capital Infusion Program grants  

[3:1:66,78] for support services to underserved business groups, as well as the Innovation Hub (iHub) and CA Made programs.  

[4:0:66,96] 0235010 - CALIFORNIA FILM COMMISSION  

[5:0:66,113] The California Film Commission (CFC) enhances California's status as the leader in motion picture, television and commercial  

[5:1:66,123] production. The Commission is tasked with retaining and increasing motion picture production and to see that it continues to  

[5:2:66,132] create jobs and boost business throughout the State. A one-stop office for filmmakers, the Commission supports productions of  

[5:3:66,142] all sizes and budgets with a variety of services. In addition to issuing film permits for all state properties, administering the film  

[5:4:66,152] and TV tax credit program, maintaining an extensive location library, and offering production assistance on a wide variety of  

[5:5:66,162] issues, CFC also works closely with cities and counties with the goal of creating 'film friendly" policies that are consistent state-

[5:6:66,171] wide.  

[6:0:66,189] 0235019 - DIVISION OF TOURISM  

[7:0:66,206] The California Tourism Market Act provides for the marketing of California through an assessment of businesses that benefit  

[7:1:66,216] from travel and tourism. The objective of the Tourism Assessment Program is to identify potentially assessable businesses,  

[7:2:66,226] assist companies with determining the appropriate amount of their self-assessment, and collet the fee.  

[8:0:66,243] 0235028 - CALIFORINIA INFRASTRUCTURE AND ECONOMIC DEVELOPMENT BANK  

[9:0:66,260] California Infrastructure and Economic Development Bank (IBank) was created to finance public infrastructure and private  

[9:1:66,270] development that promote a healthy climate for jobs, contribute to a strong economy and improve the quality of life in California  

[9:2:66,280] communities. IBank has broad authority to participate in a variety of financing transactions, including issuing tax-exempt and  

[9:3:66,289] taxable revenue bonds, providing financing to a variety of entities, providing credit enhancements, acquiring or leasing facilities,  

[9:4:66,299] and leveraging State and Federal funds. IBank's current programs include the infrastructure state revolving fund program (ISRF  

[9:5:66,309] Program), the California lending for energy and environmental needs center (CLEEN Center, a sub-program of the ISRF  

[9:6:66,319] Program), the statewide energy and efficiency program and the light emitting diode street lighting program (each a component  

[9:7:66,329] of the CLEEN Center), the bond financing program, which issues 501(c)(3)tax-exempt and taxable bonds,, industrial  

[9:8:66,338] development revenue bonds, exempt facility revenue bonds, and public agency revenue bonds.  

[10:0:66,356] 0235037 - SMALL BUSINESS LOAN GUARANTEE PROGRAM  

[11:0:66,373] The Small Business Loan Guarantee Program (SBLGP) promotes local economic development by providing guarantees for  

[11:1:66,383] loans issued to small businesses from financial institutions, typically banks, that otherwise would not approve a term loan or  

[11:2:66,392] line of credit to a small business. As a result of the SBLGP, participating small businesses are able to secure financing that  

[11:3:66,402] allows them to grow and expand their business. The loan guarantee serves as a credit enhancement and an incentive for  

[11:4:66,412] financial institutions to make loans to small businesses that otherwise would not be eligible for such financing.  

[12:0:66,429] 0235046 - CALIFORNIA WELCOME CENTERS  

[13:0:66,446] California Welcome Centers are visitor information centers that are readily accessible to and recognizable by tourists to  

[13:1:66,456] encourage tourism in California and provide benefits to the state economy. The objective of the California Welcome Center  

[13:2:66,466] Program is to determine the locality of underserved travelers, designate a welcome center, and establish operating standards  

[13:3:66,476] across the network.  

[14:0:66,493] 0240 - CALIFORNIA COMMUNITY REINVESTMENT GRANT PROGRAM 

[15:0:66,510] The California Community Reinvestment Grants (CalCRG) Program   was established on July 1, 2018   to   implement the  

[15:1:66,520] competitive grant program mandated by Proposition 64, the Adult Use of Marijuana Act, and the provisions specified in  

[15:2:66,530] Revenue and Taxation Code section 34019(d).   The CalCRG Program administers grants   for   local public   health departments  

[15:3:66,540] and qualified community-based nonprofit organizations to support various mental health treatment, substance use treatment,  

[15:4:66,549] job placement, legal services and other health and wellness-related programs for communities disproportionately affected by  

[15:5:66,559] past federal and state drug policies in California. GO-Biz must award grants annually and at least 50 percent of the grant  

[15:6:66,569] funding will be allocated to qualified community-based nonprofit organizations.  

[16:0:66,586] 0245 - LOCAL EQUITY GRANT PROGRAM  

[17:0:66,604] The Local Equity Grant Program, administered by the Governor’s Office of Business and Economic Development, will assist  

[17:1:66,613] local equity applicants or local equity licensees pursuant to subparagraphs (A) through (C), inclusive, of paragraph (2) of  

[17:2:66,623] subdivision (b) of Section 26244 of the Business and Professions Code.

[8:0:99,418] 0515   Secretary for Business, Consumer Services, and Housing Agency  

[9:0:66,439] The Business, Consumer Services, and Housing Agency (Agency) is responsible for overseeing departments, boards,  

[9:1:66,449] commissions, panels, and agencies that provide the following services to the people of California: protection of the public  

[9:2:66,458] through the licensing and regulation of more than 100 businesses and 200 professional categories; regulation of financial  

[10:0:66,468] services and state-licensed financial institutions; enforcement of the sale of alcoholic beverages and cannabis; regulation of the

[4:2:66,115] 0275 - CALIFORNIA TRAFFIC SAFETY PROGRAM  

[5:0:66,135] The California Traffic Safety Program develops the California Highway Safety Plan. The plan uses available state and federal  

[5:1:66,144] resources to identify and address major traffic safety problems throughout the state.  

[5:2:66,162] 0276 - TRANSIT AND INTERCITY RAIL CAPITAL PROGRAM  

[6:0:66,181] The Transit and Intercity Rail Capital Program provides grants to encourage low carbon transit operations through the Transit,  

[6:1:66,191] Affordable Housing, and Sustainable Communities Program. The program goals include reducing greenhouse gas emissions,  

[6:2:66,201] improving mobility access across the state, and providing benefits to California's disadvantaged communities.  

[6:3:66,218] 0277 - STATEWIDE TRANSPORTATION PRIORITIES  

[7:0:66,235] The Statewide Transportation Priorities program provides grant funding to address California’s long-term transportation goals  

[7:1:66,245] by improving California’s transportation system and helping California achieve its climate goals.

[3:0:66,68] The CalHHS accomplishes its mission through the administration and coordination of state and federal programs for public  

[3:1:66,78] health, health care services, social services, public assistance, health planning and licensing, rehabilitation, and health  

[4:0:66,88] workforce development. These programs touch the lives of millions of California's most needy and vulnerable residents. The  

[4:1:66,98] CalHHS is committed to striking a balance between maintaining access to essential health and human services for California's  

[4:2:66,108] most disadvantaged and at-risk residents while pursuing ways to better manage and control costs.

[6:3:66,269] population.  

[7:0:66,286] 0285 - THE CALIFORNIA OFFICE OF HEALTH INFORMATION INTEGRITY  

[8:0:66,306] The California Office of Health Information Integrity (CalOHII) is responsible for statewide leadership, coordination, policy  

[8:1:66,316] formation, direction, and oversight responsibilities for federal Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA)  

[8:2:66,325] requirements. As the leading resource for providing HIPAA expertise to the State of California, CalOHII exercises full authority  

[8:3:66,335] relative to state entities to establish policy, provide direction to state entities, monitor progress and report on implementation  

[8:4:66,345] efforts based on state and federal laws.

[9:2:66,399] justice system that support the youths’ successful transition into adulthood and help them become responsible, thriving, and  

[9:3:66,409] engaged members of their communities.

[2:0:164,32] 0552   Office of the Inspector General - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] The Office of the Inspector General (OIG) protects public safety by safeguarding the integrity of California's correctional  

[3:1:66,78] system. OIG is responsible for contemporaneous oversight of the California Department of Corrections and Rehabilitation's  

[3:2:66,88] (CDCR) internal affairs investigations, use of force, staff complaints, and the employee disciplinary process. The Inspector  

[3:3:66,98] General audits and reviews the policies, practices, and procedures of CDCR. The Inspector General reviews the Governor's  

[3:4:66,108] candidates for appointment to serve as warden for the state's adult correctional institutions and as superintendents for the  

[3:5:66,117] state's juvenile facilities, and conducts metric-oriented inspection programs to periodically review delivery of medical care at  

[3:6:66,127] each state prison. OIG receives communications from individuals alleging improper governmental activity and maintains a toll-

[3:7:66,137] free public telephone number to receive allegations of wrongdoing by employees of CDCR; conducts formal reviews of  

[3:8:66,147] complaints of retaliation from CDCR employees against upper management where a legally cognizable cause of action is  

[3:9:66,156] present; and reviews sexual abuse incidents within correctional institutions. OIG provides critical public transparency for the  

[3:10:66,166] state correctional system by publicly reporting its findings.  

[4:0:66,183] In addition, OIG is responsible for the California Rehabilitation Oversight Board (C-ROB) that examines CDCR's various mental  

[4:1:66,193] health, substance abuse, educational, and employment programs for incarcerated individuals and parolees. C-ROB meets at  

[4:2:66,203] least twice annually to recommend modifications, additions, and eliminations of rehabilitation and treatment programs. C-ROB  

[4:3:66,213] also submits annual reports to the Governor, the Legislature, and the public to convey its findings on the effectiveness of  

[4:4:66,223] treatment efforts, rehabilitation needs of incarcerated individuals and individuals on parole, gaps in rehabilitation services, and  

[4:5:66,232] levels of participation and success.

[5:0:175,299] 0555   Secretary for Environmental Protection  

[6:0:66,320] The Secretary for Environmental Protection is the cabinet-level agency responsible for protecting the environment. California  

[7:0:66,330] Environmental Protection Agency programs reduce greenhouse gas emissions, restore and protect environmental quality, and  

[7:1:66,340] protect public health. The Secretary coordinates the state's environmental regulatory programs and oversees the fair and  

[8:0:66,350] consistent enforcement of environmental law, which safeguards the state's residents and promotes the state's economic vitality.  

[8:1:66,359] The Secretary also administers environmental justice, environmental law enforcement, emergency preparedness and  

[9:0:66,369] response, Certified Unified Program Agencies, and scientific review programs. The Secretary leads greenhouse gas emission  

[10:0:66,379] reduction and climate change activities in state government, and is responsible for coordinating the implementation of Chapter  

[10:1:66,389] 488, Statutes of 2006 (AB 32). The Secretary also centralizes coordination of California-Mexico border environmental efforts.

[11:0:66,552] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[11:1:66,571] 0340 - SUPPORT PROGRAM  

[12:0:66,591] The Secretary for Environmental Protection's primary program objectives are restoring, protecting, and enhancing  

[12:1:66,601] environmental quality, and protecting public health while fostering economic vitality. The Secretary oversees the state's  

[12:2:66,610] environmental regulatory programs with particular emphasis on promoting "cross-media" coordination, enhancing risk  

[12:3:66,620] assessment (especially for disadvantaged communities and other sensitive populations), enforcing laws consistently and fairly,  

[12:4:66,630] and objectively measuring and reporting results.

[5:0:126,168] 0559   Secretary for Labor and Workforce Development Agency  

[5:1:66,189] The Labor and Workforce Development Agency was established to address issues relating to California workers and their  

[5:2:66,199] employers. The Agency is responsible for labor law enforcement, workforce development, and benefit payment and  

[5:3:66,209] adjudication. The Agency works to combat the underground economy and help legitimate businesses and workers in California

[4:3:66,137] for all and provides direct grant funding to projects demonstrating the value and feasibility of sustainable communities; and

[11:0:66,475] 0360 - STATE PLANNING AND POLICY DEVELOPMENT  

[12:0:66,492] By statute, OPR is the state comprehensive planning agency. The major activities of the State Planning and Policy  

[12:1:66,502] Development program can be grouped into four major categories: land use and planning, climate risk and resilience,  

[12:2:66,512] sustainable economic development, and targeted long-range research needs. More specifically these include: (1)  

[13:0:66,521] recommending and implementing state policies on land-use and growth planning and compliance with environmental statutes  

[13:1:66,531] and regulations, including General Plan Guidelines and other guidance to local and regional governments; (2) coordinating the  

[13:2:66,541] implementation of the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA), including: (a) operating the State Clearinghouse; (b)  

[13:3:66,551] maintaining an online database for the electronic submission and archiving of CEQA documents; (c) developing CEQA  

[14:0:66,561] guidelines amendments; (d) providing technical assistance; (e) providing training, and (f) coordinating SB 7 project review (3)  

[14:1:66,570] supporting the Governor's Advisor for Military Affairs and Governor's Military Council; (4) providing policy research for the  

[14:2:66,580] Governor and Cabinet; (5) supporting local planning efforts related to the impacts of droughts and wildfires;(6) supporting  

[14:3:66,590] development of state plans including, but not limited to, the Water Action Plan, the State Multi-Hazard Mitigation Plan, the  

[14:4:66,600] Safeguarding California Plan, the Integrated Energy Policy Report, the 5-Year Infrastructure Plan, and the 5th Climate  

[15:0:66,609] Assessment; (7) supporting multiple efforts to address climate change and response to carbon pollution; (8) administering the  

[15:1:66,619] Integrated Climate Adaptation and Resiliency Program to coordinate regional and local efforts with state climate adaptation  

[15:2:66,629] strategies to adapt to the impacts of climate change; (9) housing the Federal Grants Administrator for tracking of federal grants  

[15:3:66,639] coming to California and providing information on federal grants to help maximize federal grant opportunities within the state;  

[15:4:66,648] (10) administering the California Education Learning Lab, California Initiative to Advance Precision Medicine; (11) Establishing  

[15:5:66,658] and facilitating the Rural Economic Development Steering Committee/Wood Utilization Work Group to promote rural economic  

[15:6:66,668] development that drives healthy and sustainable forest management consistent with our rural economic development, public  

[15:7:66,678] health and safety, and climate goals; and (13) Per EO-N-79-20, supporting the state’s effort on a “just transition” to a carbon  

[15:8:66,688] neutral economy by 2045; (14) The Regional Early Action Planning Grants of 2021 (REAP 2.0)   which intends to help the state  

[15:9:66,697] meet its climate commitments and housing production affordability goals. REAP 2.0 funds implementation activities in adopted  

[15:10:66,707] regional and local plans that accelerate infill development, housing and reduce Vehicle Miles Traveled (VMT) in a way that  

[16:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:4:66,108] broadly accessible jobs; and (16) Conducting other activities as the Governor may direct.  

[4:0:66,125] 0365 - CALIFORNIA VOLUNTEERS  

[5:0:66,142] California Volunteers is the state office tasked with engaging Californians in services, volunteering and civic action to tackle our  

[5:1:66,152] state’s most pressing challenges while lifting up all communities. From the California Climate Action Corps, the country’s first  

[5:2:66,162] statewide climate corps program, to the #CaliforniansForAll service initiative launched in response to COVID-19 to establish a  

[5:3:66,171] volunteer corps to support the state’s response to emergencies and disasters, California Volunteers plays an integral role in  

[5:4:66,181] tackling the state’s problems. California Volunteers is led by the State’s Chief Service Officer and supported by a bipartisan  

[5:5:66,191] 25-member Commission and a team of experts driven by a mission to empower and mobilize all Californians to volunteer and  

[5:6:66,201] serve in their communities.  

[6:0:66,218] 0370 - CALIFORNIA STRATEGIC GROWTH COUNCIL  

[7:0:66,235] The California Strategic Growth Council (SGC) coordinates and works collaboratively with public agencies, communities, and  

[7:1:66,245] stakeholders to advance healthy, thriving, and resilient communities for all. SGC integrates State, regional, and local efforts to  

[7:2:66,255] reduce greenhouse gas emissions; increase the availability of affordable housing located near jobs, services, and green space;  

[7:3:66,265] conserve agriculture lands; strengthen community resilience; promote public health; and advance racial equity. SGC  

[7:4:66,274] administers the following grant programs: Affordable Housing and Sustainable Communities; Transformative Climate  

[8:0:66,284] Communities; Sustainable Agricultural Lands Conservation; Climate Change Research – all of which are part of the California  

[8:1:66,294] Climate Investments Program, funded by proceeds from the State’s cap-and-trade auction revenues. SGC operates these  

[8:2:66,304] funding programs in collaboration with interagency teams to develop program guidelines, review applications, and administer  

[8:3:66,314] program funds. SGC’s Community Assistance for Climate Equity Program encompasses both the Regional Climate  

[8:4:66,323] Collaboratives, which supports local capacity building and technical assistance in under-resourced communities across  

[8:5:66,333] California; and the California Climate Investments Technical Assistance Program, which increases access to SGC’s own grant  

[8:6:66,343] programs as well as those of many other State agencies. SGC partners with High-Speed Rail Authority (HSRA) to support  

[8:7:66,353] sustainable development and conservation practices, especially in future HSR station areas. SGC’s Health and Equity Program  

[8:8:66,362] advances the integration of health and equity principles in State programs and planning through the Health in All Policies Task  

[8:9:66,372] Force, partnerships and collaborations, and in the implementation of SGC’s Racial Equity Action Plan. SGC's Community  

[8:10:66,382] Resilience Centers Program provides grants to support communities' ability to withstand climate-related disasters and build  

[8:11:66,392] resilience year-round. Finally, SGC is charged with reviewing the State’s 5-Year Infrastructure Plan and to contribute to  

[8:12:66,401] interagency efforts to promote sustainability, equity, and resilience in State investments.  

[9:0:66,419] 0371 - OFFICE OF COMMUNITY PARTNERSHIPS AND STRATEGIC COMMUNICATIONS  

[10:0:66,436] The Office of Community Partnerships and Strategic Communications (OCPSC) manages the State’s highest priority  

[10:1:66,446] community engagement and public awareness efforts and will be initially focused on COVID-19 vaccines and climate justice  

[10:2:66,456] such as water conservation. OCPSC works with respective state agencies and departments to inform outreach campaign  

[10:3:66,465] efforts and support greater coordination and collaboration within state government. OCPSC recognizes the vital role public-

[10:4:66,475] private partners and community partners play in helping to mobilize coordinated outreach efforts to address the State’s most  

[10:5:66,485] pressing issues. In partnership with an ecosystem of trusted messengers, including ethnic media partners, OCPSC directly  

[10:6:66,495] engages Californians, including those experiencing the greatest health and social inequities, with culturally competent and  

[10:7:66,504] actionable information.

[12:0:202,465] 0690   Office of Emergency Services  

[13:0:66,486] The principal objective of the Office of Emergency Services (Cal OES) is to protect lives and property, build emergency  

[13:1:66,496] response capabilities, and support communities for a resilient California. The Cal OES Director serves as both the Governor's  

[13:2:66,505] Homeland Security Advisor and Emergency Management Director, with responsibility to implement and facilitate the state's  

[13:3:66,515] homeland security and counter-terrorism strategy. Cal OES serves the public through effective collaboration in preparing for,  

[13:4:66,525] protecting against, responding to, recovering from, and mitigating the impacts of hazards and threats.  

[13:5:66,542] Cal OES provides leadership, assistance, training, and support to state and local agencies and coordinates with federal  

[13:6:66,552] agencies in planning and preparing for the most effective use of federal, state, local, and private sector resources in  

[13:7:66,562] emergencies. This emergency planning is based upon a system of mutual aid whereby a jurisdiction relies first on its own  

[13:8:66,571] resources, and then requests assistance from its neighbors. Cal OES' plans and programs are coordinated with those of the  

[13:9:66,581] federal government, other states, private sector, utilities, and state and local agencies within California.  

[13:10:66,599] During an emergency, Cal OES functions as the Governor's immediate staff to provide guidance and coordinate the state's  

[13:11:66,608] responsibilities under the Emergency Services Act and applicable federal statutes. It also acts as the conduit for federal  

[13:12:66,618] assistance through natural disaster grants and federal agency support. Additionally, Cal OES is responsible for the  

[13:13:66,628] development and coordination of a comprehensive state strategy related to all hazards, including terrorism, which includes  

[13:14:66,638] prevention, preparedness, mitigation, response, and recovery.  

[14:0:66,655] Cal OES implements the state's homeland security strategy by overseeing the California Cybersecurity Integration Center and  

[14:1:66,665] the State Threat Assessment System (STAS), which includes management of the State Threat Assessment Center. The STAS  

[14:2:66,674] assists in the detection, prevention, and investigation of   and response to criminal and terrorist activity and   also facilitates  

[14:3:66,684] information and intelligence sharing between local, state, federal, tribal agencies, and private sector partners.  

[15:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,68] The Alfred E. Alquist Seismic Safety   Commission   is a separate unit within the   Office of Emergency Services. Its mission is to  

[3:1:66,78] lower earthquake risk to life and property of Californians. The Commission works with federal, state, and local agencies, as well  

[3:2:66,88] as the private sector, on a variety of activities that guide and stimulate earthquake risk reduction and management.  

[4:0:66,105] Because Cal OES' programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, Cal OES has a capital outlay program to support this  

[4:1:66,115] need. For the specifics on Cal OES' capital outlay program, see "Infrastructure Overview."

[0:0:66,13] 2023-24 STATE BUDGET — LJE   122 

[1:0:382,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[2:0:167,32] 0690   Office of Emergency Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,65] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:0:66,84] 0380 - EMERGENCY MANAGEMENT SERVICES  

[5:0:66,103] Working through the state's mutual aid system, the Emergency Management Services and Homeland Security Program  

[5:1:66,113] coordinates the provision   of federal, state, and local resources to jurisdictions whose resources and services are overextended  

[5:2:66,123] in a disaster situation. In addition, this program develops and coordinates a comprehensive state strategy related to an all-

[5:3:66,133] hazards approach that includes prevention, preparedness, mitigation, response, and recovery consistent with the National  

[5:4:66,142] Strategy on Homeland Security. Central to this effort is maintaining operational readiness at all levels of government. Within this  

[5:5:66,152] program, Cal OES also trains emergency managers, responders, and state and local leaders in preparedness and response to  

[5:6:66,162] all hazards.  

[6:0:66,179] 0385 - SPECIAL PROGRAMS AND GRANT MANAGEMENT  

[7:0:66,196] Cal OES serves as the State Administering Agent for federal homeland security, emergency management, and victim services  

[7:1:66,206] grants and is the primary liaison with the Federal Emergency Management Agency, the United States Department of Homeland  

[7:2:66,216] Security, and other federal agencies. Additionally, Cal OES serves as an advocate for local public safety, emergency  

[7:3:66,226] management, and public and private agencies operating public safety and victim service programs. As part of its grant  

[7:4:66,236] management role, Cal OES administers the California Disaster Assistance Act and provides eligible local agencies with  

[7:5:66,245] financial assistance to recover from disasters. Included in this program is the State Threat Assessment Center, which is the  

[7:6:66,255] centerpiece of the state's intelligence information sharing environment and serves as the Governor's designated primary fusion  

[7:7:66,265] center.  

[8:0:66,282] 0390 - ALFRED E. ALQUIST SEISMIC SAFETY COMMISSION  

[9:0:66,299] The Alfred E. Alquist Seismic Safety Commission program provides a coordinated framework for establishing consistent  

[9:1:66,309] earthquake policies; advising the Governor, the Legislature, local governments, and the public; and tracking the state’s  

[9:2:66,319] progress toward higher levels of seismic safety.   The Commission uses the expertise of its commissioners to review, evaluate,  

[9:3:66,329] and translate scientific information and make recommendations to guide and influence earthquake safety policies.   The  

[9:4:66,339] Commission works with federal, state, and local agencies, as well as the private sector, on a variety of activities that support  

[9:5:66,348] the state’s earthquake preparedness, mitigation, response, and recovery efforts.   These activities include: (1) developing and  

[9:6:66,358] reviewing seismic safety projects; (2) providing consistent policy direction; (3) proposing and reviewing earthquake-related  

[9:7:66,368] legislation; (4) conducting public hearings on seismic safety issues; (5) using existing knowledge and conducting studies,  

[9:8:66,378] where necessary, to improve the performance of structures in California, (6) recommending earthquake safety programs and  

[9:9:66,387] supporting cost-effective partnerships that help reduce earthquake risks and speed economic recovery.  

[9:10:66,405] 0395 - PUBLIC SAFETY COMMUNICATIONS  

[10:0:66,424] The Public Safety Communications   program is responsible for the design, installation, maintenance, and repair of the  

[10:1:66,434] state's   public safety communications networks and oversight of the state's 9-1-1 system. The   program is dedicated to the  

[10:2:66,444] preservation and protection of human life and public safety by delivering reliable and dependable communication services that  

[10:3:66,454] keep the public connected during times of crisis.  

[10:4:66,471] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION AND EXECUTIVE  

[11:0:66,490] The Administration and Executive Program provides the overall policy direction of   Cal OES and support services such as  

[11:1:66,500] accounting, fiscal, personnel, information technology, and business services.

[3:0:66,89] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW  

[4:0:66,108] The Office of Emergency Services' infrastructure includes a headquarters facility, an administrative building, and an Inland  

[4:1:66,117] Regional Operations Center in Sacramento County; a Coastal Regional Operations Center in Fairfield in Solano County; a  

[4:2:66,127] Southern Regional Operations Center located at Los Alamitos Joint Forces Training Base in Orange County; the California  

[4:3:66,137] Specialized Training Institute at Camp San Luis Obispo; and various small field offices throughout the state.  

[4:4:66,154] The Public Safety Communications division (PSC) is comprised of a main leased complex in Sacramento and 48 field locations  

[4:5:66,164] throughout the state. These locations include 7 area offices and 41 area shops, positioned geographically to facilitate  

[4:6:66,174] maintenance and installation services to remote communication sites and customers throughout the state. In addition, the PSC  

[4:7:66,184] maintains and operates 11 communications vaults/towers and a total of more than 3,500 radio frequency points of presence.

[7:0:191,295] 0750   Office of the Lieutenant Governor  

[8:0:66,316] Under California's Constitution, the Lieutenant Governor serves as Acting Governor whenever the Governor is absent from the  

[8:1:66,325] state, and automatically becomes Governor if a vacancy occurs in the Office of Governor. The Lieutenant Governor is also  

[8:2:66,335] President of the Senate and votes in case of a tie.  

[9:0:66,352] The Lieutenant Governor serves as a voting member of the Board of Regents of the University of California, the Board of  

[9:1:66,362] Trustees of the California State University system, and the Board of Governors of the California Community Colleges system.  

[9:2:66,372] The Lieutenant Governor also sits on the Calbright College Board of Trustees.  

[9:3:66,389] The Lieutenant Governor also serves on, and rotates with the State Controller, as chair of the three-member State Lands  

[9:4:66,399] Commission, which oversees the control and leasing of millions of acres of state-owned land, including offshore oil resources,  

[9:5:66,409] as well as use and permitting for all navigable waterways in California. The Commission also manages state land-use planning  

[9:6:66,419] and revenues, and related interstate issues. During alternate years, when the Lieutenant Governor serves as Chairperson of  

[9:7:66,428] the State Lands Commission, the Lieutenant Governor also serves as a member of the Ocean Protection Council   and as a  

[9:8:66,438] non-voting member of the California Coastal Commission.  

[10:0:66,455] In addition, under state statutes, the Lieutenant Governor chairs the California Commission for Economic Development, which  

[10:1:66,465] provides support and guidance to the Governor, Legislature, and private sector regarding the development of California's  

[10:2:66,475] economy.

[8:0:224,300] 0820   Department of Justice  

[9:0:66,321] The constitutional office of the Attorney General, as chief law officer of the state, has the responsibility to see that the laws of  

[9:1:66,331] California are uniformly and adequately enforced. This responsibility is fulfilled through the diverse programs of the Department  

[9:2:66,341] of Justice.  

[10:0:66,360] The Department of Justice is responsible for providing skillful and efficient legal services on behalf of the people of California.  

[10:1:66,370] The Attorney General represents the people in all matters before the Appellate and Supreme Courts of California and the  

[10:2:66,380] United States; serves as legal counsel to state officers, boards, commissioners, and departments; represents the people in  

[10:3:66,390] actions to protect the environment and to enforce consumer, antitrust, and civil laws; and assists district attorneys in the  

[11:0:66,400] administration of justice. The Department provides oversight, enforcement, education, and regulation of California's firearms/ 

[11:1:66,409] dangerous weapon laws; provides evaluation and analysis of physical evidence; regulates legal gambling activities in  

[12:0:66,419] California; supports the telecommunications and data processing needs of the California criminal justice community; and  

[12:1:66,429] pursues projects designed to protect the people of California from fraudulent, unfair, and illegal activities.

[5:0:66,536] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,554] 0435 - LEGAL SERVICES  

[6:0:66,574] Legal Services is organized into four elements: (1) Civil Law, (2) Criminal Law,   (3) Public Rights, and (4) Medi-Cal and Elder  

[6:1:66,584] Abuse.  

[7:0:66,603] Civil Law represents the State of California and its officers, agencies, departments, boards, commissions, and employees in  

[7:1:66,613] civil matters. It provides advice to these clients, defends cases brought against them, prosecutes cases to vindicate state  

[8:0:66,623] interests, and conducts investigations. Deputy Attorneys General in Civil Law are responsible for managing and litigating cases  

[8:1:66,633] before administrative tribunals, and in both state and federal courts at the trial level and on appeal, including appeals before the  

[8:2:66,642] United States and California Supreme Courts. Deputies work in one of   nine sections: Business Litigation; Cannabis Control;  

[8:3:66,652] Correctional Law; Employment and Administrative Mandate; Government Law; Health, Education, and Welfare; Health Quality  

[8:4:66,662] Enforcement; Licensing; and Tort and Condemnation.  

[9:0:66,682] Criminal Law represents the   People of the State of California   in criminal matters before the Appellate and Supreme courts.  

[9:1:66,691] Criminal Law also fulfills the Attorney General's responsibilities of assisting district attorneys in cases for which they are  

[10:0:66,701] recused, conducting criminal investigations, representing the Governor, Board of Parole Hearings, and California Department of  

[10:1:66,711] Corrections and Rehabilitation in state and federal habeas corpus cases and appeals, and other proceedings relating to parole  

[11:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

# === PAGE 145 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:66,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:410,13] 2023-24 STATE BUDGET — LJE   143 

[2:0:189,32] 0820   Department of Justice - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] decisions and conditions of confinement in the state prisons, and defending criminal judgements in state and federal habeas  

[3:1:66,78] corpus matters. Additional responsibilities include enforcing the Political Reform Act, advising the Governor on extradition  

[3:2:66,88] matters, and investigating, prosecuting, and coordinating litigation involving white-collar crimes, high-tech/computer/privacy  

[3:3:66,98] crimes, financial crimes, human trafficking, environmental crimes, public corruption, and officer-involved shootings.  

[4:0:66,117] Public Rights protects and preserves the public’s interests by providing legal services to state agencies, boards and  

[4:1:66,127] commissions, and Constitutional Officers, and by bringing actions in the name of the Attorney General to protect the public.  

[4:2:66,137] Public Rights provides specialized services in the following areas: Civil Rights Enforcement (including the Bureau of Children's  

[4:3:66,147] Justice); Racial Justice; Disability Rights; Worker Rights and Fair Labor; Charitable Trusts Enforcement and Regulation  

[4:4:66,156] (including the Registry of Charitable Trusts); Natural Resources Law; Corporate Fraud (including False Claims, Energy and  

[4:5:66,166] Corporate Responsibility); Healthcare Rights and Access (including Tobacco Litigation and Enforcement, and Healthcare  

[4:6:66,176] Competition and Pharmaceutical pricing); Indian and Gaming Law; Environment Law (including the Bureau of Environmental  

[4:7:66,186] Justice); Land Use and Conservation; Consumer Protection (including Privacy Enforcement and Sellers of Travel); and Antitrust  

[4:8:66,196] Law.  

[5:0:66,213] The Division of Medi-Cal Fraud and Elder Abuse represents the People of the State of California in both criminal and civil  

[5:1:66,223] matters involving Medi-Cal provider fraud, the abuse or neglect of elder and dependent adults in residential facilities, and the  

[5:2:66,232] abuse and neglect of Medi-Cal recipients in non-institutional settings. The Division is a vertical prosecution unit whose  

[5:3:66,242] investigations are conducted by multidisciplinary teams consisting of Special Agents, Investigative Auditors, Digital Forensic  

[5:4:66,252] Specialists, Registered Nurses, and Deputy Attorneys General. Deputy Attorneys General from the Division represent the  

[5:5:66,262] People of the State of California in both federal and state courts. Types of cases frequently prosecuted by the Division include  

[5:6:66,271] fraud committed against the Medi-Cal program by doctors, pharmacies, clinics, dentists, medical equipment suppliers, hospice,  

[5:7:66,281] home health companies, and all other Medi-Cal providers; elder or dependent adult abuse or neglect in skilled nursing facilities,  

[5:8:66,291] residential care facilities for the elderly, intermediate care facilities for the developmentally disabled, and other specified  

[5:9:66,301] residential care facilities; and the neglect or abuse of Medi-Cal recipients in non-institutional settings, when such abuse or  

[5:10:66,311] neglect is connected to the provision of case.  

[6:0:66,328] 0440 - LAW ENFORCEMENT  

[7:0:66,347] The Division of Law Enforcement is organized into five areas: (1) Bureau of Firearms, (2) Bureau of Forensic Services, (3)  

[7:1:66,357] Bureau of Gambling Control, (4) Bureau of Investigation, and (5) the Office of the Chief.  

[8:0:66,377] The Bureau of Firearms (BOF) provides oversight, enforcement, education, and regulation of California's firearms and  

[8:1:66,386] ammunition   laws by administering a multitude of different state-mandated firearms and ammunition-related programs. It is  

[8:2:66,396] accomplished by conducting firearm and ammunition eligibility checks, conducting compliance inspections at firearm dealers,  

[8:3:66,406] ammunition vendors, and manufacturers, and by providing valuable training to stakeholders statewide. BOF Special Agents  

[8:4:66,416] conduct investigations on armed and prohibited persons and other investigations resulting in the seizure of firearms,  

[8:5:66,426] magazines, and ammunition. Finally, BOF Special Agents conduct investigations to monitor and   prevent illegal   firearm  

[8:6:66,435] trafficking at permitted gun shows in accordance with state and federal laws.  

[9:0:66,455] The Bureau of Forensic Services (BFS) provides evaluation and scientific analysis of physical evidence, crime scene  

[9:1:66,465] investigation, and scientific investigative support for officer-involved shooting investigations. Additionally BFS provides expert  

[9:2:66,474] court testimony to federal, state and local law enforcement agencies, district attorneys, and courts. The BFS operates 10  

[9:3:66,484] regional crime laboratories and two specialized laboratories, the Jan Bashinski DNA Laboratory and Statewide Toxicology  

[9:4:66,494] Laboratory, which   serve 46 of California’s 58 counties. The BFS also operates the California Criminalistics Institute forensic  

[9:5:66,504] training facility that provides training for forensic scientists worldwide. Finally, BFS maintains the state DNA database, which  

[9:6:66,514] stores and regularly searches the DNA profiles of sex and violent offenders and felony arrestees against the DNA profiles of  

[9:7:66,523] evidence from unsolved crimes.  

[10:0:66,543] The Bureau of Gambling Control (BGC) regulates legal gambling activities in California to ensure gambling is conducted  

[10:1:66,553] honestly and is free from criminal and corruptive elements. This is accomplished by investigating the qualifications of  

[10:2:66,562] individuals and business entities who apply for licenses and monitoring the conduct of these licensees to ensure compliance  

[10:3:66,572] with the Gambling Control Act and applicable regulations. BGC conducts criminal investigations in and around tribal casinos  

[10:4:66,582] and California cardrooms. In addition, BGC conducts audits and reviews for tribal gaming to ensure that each tribe is in  

[10:5:66,592] compliance with all aspects of the state gaming compact.  

[11:0:66,611] The Bureau of Investigation (BI) is the premiere investigative bureau that is responsible for investigating and dismantling  

[11:1:66,621] criminal organizations, as well as assisting with the prosecution of serious criminal offenses that present a significant and multi-

[11:2:66,631] jurisdictional threat to California. The BI prioritizes investigations related to transnational criminal enterprises involved in gangs,  

[11:3:66,641] as well as cases involving major white-collar fraud, underground economy, recycle fraud, officer-involved shootings, homicides,  

[11:4:66,650] foreign prosecution, human trafficking and sexual predator apprehension crimes. In addition, BI serves a principal role in  

[11:5:66,660] providing leadership, coordination, and support to law enforcement through intelligence support centers and multi-agency task  

[11:6:66,670] forces focusing on violent offenders, gangs, and major crimes statewide.  

[12:0:66,689] The Office of the Chief (Office) provides administrative support to the investigative, regulatory, and forensic components of the  

[12:1:66,699] Division of Law Enforcement and other criminal justice agencies. The Office serves as the policy-making and oversight body for  

[12:2:66,709] its four operational bureaus.  

[13:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,68] 0445 - CALIFORNIA JUSTICE INFORMATION SERVICES  

[4:0:66,88] The California Justice Information Services Division provides criminal justice intelligence, information, and identification  

[4:1:66,98] services to law enforcement, regulatory agencies, and the public. Four major functional areas carry out these primary services:  

[4:2:66,108] 1) The Justice Data and Investigative Services Bureau consolidates the identification, investigative, and field services functions,  

[4:3:66,117] providing information and technical assistance on manual and automated systems including the fingerprint identification system  

[4:4:66,127] and the violent crime information system; 2) The Bureau of Criminal Information and Analysis consolidates the functions related  

[4:5:66,137] to the authorization, release, and use of criminal offender record information for law enforcement investigatory and regulatory  

[4:6:66,147] purposes; 3) The Hawkins Data Center operates the Criminal Justice Information System and the California Law Enforcement  

[4:7:66,156] Telecommunications System, as well as provides IT services for the Attorney General’s Office; 4) the Operations Support  

[4:8:66,166] Program provides business resumption planning and administrative support and oversight; and 5) the Department of Justice  

[4:9:66,176] Research Center, within the Operations Support Program, oversees statistical models and engages in the analysis of data to  

[4:10:66,186] provide evidence-based research.  

[5:0:66,203] 9900 - DIRECTORATE AND ADMINISTRATION  

[6:0:66,220] The Directorate and the Administration Division of the Department of Justice consists of the Attorney General's Executive  

[6:1:66,230] Office and the Division of Operations. The Executive Office maintains the overall direction and administration of the diverse  

[6:2:66,240] programs and projects of the department, including the Equal Employment Rights and Resolution Office, the Office of Program  

[6:3:66,250] Oversight and Accountability, the Opinions Unit, the Solicitor General's Unit, the Office of Legislative Affairs, the Office of  

[6:4:66,259] Communications, the Public Inquiry Unit, and the Office of Community Awareness, Response, and Engagement. In addition,  

[6:5:66,269] the Division of Operations provides support functions essential to the department's operations, including fiscal, personnel, and  

[6:6:66,279] specialized business services such as legal secretarial support, litigation support, legal case management services, and  

[6:7:66,289] facilities management.

[2:0:207,32] 0840   State Controller - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] The State Controller is the chief fiscal officer of California. Principally responsible for transparency and accountability of the  

[4:0:66,78] state's financial resources, the Controller ensures the appropriate disbursement and tracking of taxpayer dollars. The Controller  

[4:1:66,88] serves on dozens of state boards, commissions, and committees with duties   ranging from   administrative oversight of the  

[5:0:66,98] nation's two largest public pension funds,   to protection of state lands and coastlines,   to modernization and financing of major  

[5:1:66,108] infrastructure. The Controller also offers fiscal guidance to local governments and has independent auditing authority over  

[5:2:66,117] government agencies related to the spending of state funds. The Controller's primary objectives are to:  

[6:0:65,135] • Account for and control disbursement of all state funds, issuing warrants in payment of the state's bills.  

[6:1:65,150] • Determine legality and accuracy of financial claims against the state.  

[6:2:65,166] • Audit state and local government programs and agencies.  

[7:0:65,182] • Ensure businesses report and remit unclaimed property in compliance with Unclaimed Property Law and safeguard remitted  

[7:1:76,192] unclaimed property until claimed by the rightful owners or heirs.  

[7:2:65,207] • Inform the public of the state's financial condition.  

[8:0:65,223] • Inform the public of financial transactions of city, county, and other local governments.  

[8:1:65,239] • Administer the Uniform State Payroll System.  

[9:0:65,255] • Audit and process all personnel and payroll transactions for state civil service, state exempt employees, California State  

[9:1:76,265] University employees, and Judicial Council employees.

[10:0:66,391] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[11:0:66,410] 0500100 - ACCOUNTING AND REPORTING  

[12:0:66,429] The State Accounting and Reporting Division maintains uniform and systematic control accounts of all receipts, payments,  

[12:1:66,439] appropriations, state fund balances, and bonded indebtedness; monitors the cash flow of the General Fund; administers the  

[12:2:66,449] statewide discharge from accountability program; participates in offsetting monies owed to the state; reports the financial  

[12:3:66,458] condition of the state; and collaborates with the Department of Finance, the State Treasurer, and the Department of General  

[12:4:66,468] Services to develop and implement the Financial Information System for California (FI$Cal) to ensure the system meets the  

[12:5:66,478] state's primary objectives and provides best business practices for the state.  

[13:0:66,498] The Local Government Programs and Services Division maintains a database of information and reports on local financial  

[13:1:66,507] transactions and government compensation; apportions shared revenues to local governments; administers local mandated  

[13:2:66,517] and non-mandated cost reimbursement programs; approves county cost allocation plans; prescribes uniform accounting  

[13:3:66,527] procedures for counties, special districts, and trial court revenues; plans and facilitates an annual conference with county  

[13:4:66,537] auditors; administers and collects estate and inheritance taxes; collects delinquent insurance and motor vehicle fuel taxes,  

[13:5:66,546] petroleum and gas assessments, and trial court penalties; refunds gasoline taxes paid on fuel consumed for off-highway  

[13:6:66,556] purposes; instructs and advises county tax collectors; approves state and local government requests to participate in the  

[13:7:66,566] Interagency Intercept Collection Program; collects recorder fees from counties pursuant to the Building Homes and Jobs Act,  

[13:8:66,576] (Chapter 364, Statutes of 2017); and administers the Property Tax Postponement Program for seniors and people who are  

[13:9:66,586] blind or have a disability.  

[14:0:66,603] 0500200 - AUDITS  

[15:0:66,622] The Audits Division determines the legality and accuracy of all claims against the state through the performance of prepayment  

[15:1:66,632] audits; assures the accuracy of local government claims and financial statements submitted to the state and federal  

[15:2:66,642] governments by establishing and updating audit guidelines, and reviewing audits performed by independent auditors; performs  

[15:3:66,652] field audits for state and federal programs; reviews the single audit reports of local governments and local education agencies  

[15:4:66,661] that receive pass-through federal funds from state agencies; and audits major businesses for compliance with the Unclaimed  

[15:5:66,671] Property Law.  

[16:0:66,689] 0500300 - PERSONNEL AND PAYROLL SERVICES  

[17:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.
